EBS/00/133 CONFIDENTIAL July 10, 2000  

To: Members of the Executive Board  

From: The Secretary  

# Subject:  

# Chad—Staff Report for the 2000 Article IV Consultation, First Review Under the Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility, and Request for Waiver of Performance Criteria  

Attached for consideration by the Executive Directors is the staff report for the 2000 Article IV consultation with Chad, the first review under the Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility, and Chad's request for a waiver of performance criteria. A draft decision appears on pages 25 and 26. This subject, together the preliminary document for the enhanced HIPC Initiative for Chad (EBS/00/125, 6/29/00), and the Assessment of the Interim Poverty Reduction Strategy Paper and the Interim Poverty Reduction Strategy Paper for Chad (EBD/00/55, 7/10/o0), is tentatively scheduled for discussion on Monday, July 24, 2000.  

Mr. E. Harris (ext. 3662l) and Mr. Ntungwanayo (ext. 37128) are available to answer technical or factual questions relating to this paper prior to the Board discussion.  

Unless the Documents Section (ext. 36760) is otherwise notified, the document will be transmitted, in accordance with the procedures approved by the Executive Board and with the appropriate deletions, to the WTO Secretariat on Tuesday, July 18, 2000; and to the African Development Bank, the European Commission, and the Islamic Development Bank, following its consideration by the Executive Board.

# INTERNATIONALMONETARYFUND  

# CHAD  

# Staff Report for the 20o0 Article IV Consultation and the First Review of the First Annual Arrangement Under the Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility and Request for Waiver of Performance Criteria  

Prepared by the African Department  

Approved by Amor Tahari and Anthony Boote  

In consultation with the Fiscal Affairs, Legal, Monetary and Exchange Affairs, Policy Development and Review, Statistics, and Treasurer's Departments)  

July 10, 2000  

The discussions on the 2000 Article IV consultation and the first review of the first annual arrangement under the Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility (PRGF) were held in N'Djamena during May 5-21, 2000.   
The staff team consisted of Mr. Harris (head), Mr. Ntungwanayo, Mr. Guillaume, Ms. Allain (EP), Ms. Da Luz, and Ms. Lefever (Assistant) (all AFR), and Mr. Fiator, the Fund's Resident Representative in Chad. Mr. Caller and Ms. Keane of the World Bank participated fully in the mission. Mr. Barro-Chambrier, Executive Director for Chad, joined the mission during the second week and participated fully in discussions during his stay.   
The Chadian representatives in these discussions included Mr. Yamoussoum, the Prime Minister; Mr. Hassan, Minister of Finance; Mr. Lamine, Minister of Economic Promotion and   
Development; Mr. Bichara, Minister of Transport and Public Works; Mr. Ben Barka, the National Director of the Bank of Central African States (BEAC); and other senior officials. The mission also met with the high Interministerial Committee. The Executive Director, the Mission Chief, and the Resident Representative were also received by the President.   
The three-year PRGF arrangement, in an amount equivalent to SDR 36.4 million (65 percent of quota Eleventh General Review of Quotas) was approved by the Executive Board on January 7, 2000. under the proposed Board decision, a further disbursement, the third of the arrangement, would be available upon completion of the third review, scheduled for January 20oo, based on the performance criteria at end-September 20o0. If all disbursements and repayments under the new PRGF arrangements are made as scheduled, Chad's outstanding use of Fund resources would rise from SDR 50.2 million (89.6 percent of quota) at end-November 1999 to   
SDR 77.7 milion (138.8 percent of quota) at end-December 2002.   
In completing the 1999 Article IV consultation, along with the midterm review under the third annual ESAF arrangement on March 29, 1999, Executive Directors noted the improvement in fiscal performance and implementation of structural reforms despite difficult economic   
conditions. They urged the authorities to sustain their efforts to accelerate fiscal consolidation and the implementation of the privatization program.

# EXECUTIVE SUMMARY  

# Developments and program implementation in 1999-2000  

The outturn at end-1999 in terms of growth, inflation, and the external current account was within program parameters. A renewed deterioration of the energy situation at the start of 2000 has adversely affected economic activity and imports. Projected growth for 2000 has thus been revised downward from 3.8 percent to 1 percent.   
The public finances deteriorated in 1999, due to the adverse impact of the energy crisis in the first half of the year, but the outcome in the first quarter of 2000 was broadly in line with the program's objectives in terms of the primary current and overall balances-—however, revenue composition differed from expectations, and social and capital spending was well below the targeted levels.   
Considerable progress was made in structural reforms. The privatization program has advanced; agreement was reached on the structure of road maintenance, preparations for the reform of the civil service statutes have moved forward; the system of petroleum product prices was reformed. Various aspects of the reform of the cotton sector were also implemented.   
Most of the performance criteria and benchmarks for end-March 2oo0 were met. However, waivers have been requested for three performance criteria that were not observed at end-March 20oo: (i) the quantitative criterion on the reduction of domestic arrears was not met; (ii) the structural criterion on the adoption of a treasury cash flow plan was completed 10 days late; and (iii) the structural criterion on the adoption of a financial rehabilitation plan and the nomination of a controller-general for the cotton company was delayed, in part owing to the late mobilization of the expected external financing. The targets for the rest of the year have been revised accordingly.  

# The policy discussions  

The economic outlook for the rest of the year depends critically on resolving the energy crisis and re-establishing regular supplies of electricity and fuel. A rational policy for adequate security stocks would be a priority.   
The energy crisis is likely to have an adverse impact on revenues during the rest of the year. The reforms of the tax and customs administration should be pursued diligently, particularly the implementation of the SYDONIA customs system. Effective revenue mobilization must be carefully monitored, and the treasury cashflow plan used to for the effective management of expenditure commitments. Steps must be taken to ensure that social and investment expenditures are executed as planned.  

In the structural area, the mission recommended: (i) the full liberalization of petroleum prices, and the conversion of the part of the petroleum tax earmarked for road maintenance into a user fee, as originally envisaged; (ii) the acceleration of the preparations for the civil service reform in time for the next budget year; (iii) careful preparation of the administrative decentralization to prevent any loss of financial discipline; and maintaining the momentum of cotton sector reform. The process of preparing the poverty reduction strategy has started well. The authorities now need to identify their requirements of financial and technical assistance and seek commitments from their partners.  

# Issues raised in the staff appraisal  

The importance of resolving the energy situation, and avoiding recurrent interruptions in energy and fuel supplies. ? The importance of reinforcing customs performance through the introduction of the SYDONIA system, and continuing the reform of the tax administration, while monitoring monthly revenue mobilization closely. Steps should be taken to avoid further shortfalls in social spending and public investment, while adjusting overall expenditures as necessary on the basis of the treasury cash-flow plan. The need for the diversification of the deposit base and loan structure of the commercial banks, and developing a microfinance system to provide access to smallscale credit and mobilize savings. The need to maintain the momentum of the structural reform program, particularly in the civil service and cotton sector, and to avoid any weakening of fiscal discipline through the administrative decentralization program.

# I. INTRODUCTION  

1. In a letter to the Managing Director dated May 31, 2000, and in the accompanying memorandum of economic and financial policies (MEFP) (Appendix I, Attachment), the government of Chad describes the implementation of its economic program for the period October 1999-September 2000, supported by the Fund under the three-year Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility (PRGF) arrangement approved on January 7, 2000, as well as the steps it intends to follow to ensure the attainment of the objectives for the rest of the period covered under the first year of the arrangement.  

2. The World Bank's current assistance program in Chad was laid out in the 2000 Country Assistance Strategy (CAS), presented to the Bank's Board in May 2000. The new CAS is predicated on the development and exploitation of Chad's oil resources--a project in support of the construction of a pipeline from Chad to the Atlantic coast of Cameroon was approved by the Bank's Board on June 6, 2000.' A major capacity-building project to facilitate the transition to the oil era was approved by the Bank's Board on January 27, 2000. A health sector credit was approved in April 2000, and a transport sector adjustment credit is also under preparation. Chad relations with the Fund and with the World Bank are presented in Appendices II and III, respectively.  

# II. ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENTS AND PROGRAM IMPLEMENTATION IN 1999-2000  

3. Chad's implementation of the new PRGF arrangement has been broadly satisfactory. The outturn at end-1999 in terms of growth, inflation, and the external current account were within program parameters. Although the public finance outturn at end-1999 fell well below program targets, this largely reflected the adverse impact of the energy crisis in the first half of the year. The monetary objectives of the program were met, and considerable progress was made in implementing the structural reform agenda.  

4.Most of the performance criteria and benchmarks at the end of the first quarter of 2000 were observed. However, one quantitative and two structural performance criteria at end-March 20o0 were missed. The quantitative criterion on the minimum repayment of domestic arrears was not met, owing to the need to provide liquidity support to the water and electricity company (STEE, see below) and the non-reimbursement by the sugar company of external debt service paid on its behalf by the government. One of the two missed structural criteria, the adoption of a cash flow plan for the treasury, was completed ten days late because of administrative delays linked to a cabinet reshuffle. The other measure--the adoption of a financial rehabilitation plan for the cotton company (COTONTCHAD) and the nomination of a controller-general to execute it-was delayed by the late release of expected external financing for the required operational audit.  

# A. Developments in the Real Sector  

5. Real GDP contracted by an estimated 0.7 percent in 1999 under the influence of two exogenous factors: the return to normal levels of agricultural production after the weather-related bumper food crop harvest of 1998; and the negative impact on production of the severe energy crisis that Chad experienced from the last quarter of 1998 into the first quarter of 1999 (Table 2). Food crop production fell by 13.7 percent in 1999 (relative to the record levels attained in the 1998 crop season), while cotton production declined by 6.6 percent. At the same time, the sharp contraction in cotton ginning in 1999 resulting from the relatively small volumes of cotton produced the year before, together with the impact of the energy crisis on manufacturing, lowered manufacturing output. By contrast, production increased in all areas of the tertiary sector (see Figure 1).  

6. The energy situation again deteriorated at the beginning of 2000, as the financial problems of STEE were compounded by uncertain supplies of petroleum imports, culminating in the total interruption of imports for three weeks in April-May 2000.² The shortage of fuel for private generators and transport trucks has depressed production and imports thus far in 2000, with significant ramifications for the outlook for growth for the rest of the year." Given the difficulties anticipated in restoring normal levels of electricity generation, production in the secondary sector is projected to contract sharply (by some 9 percent) over the course of 20o0, and production in the tertiary sector is expected to stagnate. Real GDP is thus projected to grow by only about 1 percent for the year as whole.  

.三.  

7.The consumer price index declined by 8 percent in 1999, reflecting primarily the food crop surplus; however, transportation prices rose in the last quarter, in part owing to higher import prices of petroleum. The consumer price index fell by a further 1.5 percent in the first quarter of 20o0, following the usual seasonal trend and reflecting abundant food supplies, but average inflation in 2000 is now projected at 3.7 percent (compared with the original projection of 2.3 percent). The GDP deflator fell by 4.3 percent in 1999 and is now projected to rise by 3.l percent in 2000.  

8. The ratio of gross fixed capital formation to GDP reached the equivalent of 13.4 percent in 1999 (12.9 percent in 1998) and is projected to fall to 12.9 percent in 2000, despite higher nominal public investment. Domestic consumption increased by almost 8 percent of GDP, accommodated by the drawdown of surplus stocks of food crops. Gross domestic savings consequently fell from 4.3 percent of GDP in 1998 to a dissaving of 3.0 percent in 1999 (Table 3 and Figure 2).  

# B. Public Finances  

9. The public finance situation deteriorated in 1999 (Table 4). Revenue was at roughly the same level as in 1998, but primary expenditures were considerably higher—the primary current balance thus shifted from a surplus of 1.l percent of GDP in 1998 to a small deficit of CFAF 1.4 billion ( $_{-0.2}$ percent of GDP) in 1999, compared with a programmed surplus of 0.9 percent of GDP. With the sharp increase in public investment and the repayment of 0.5 percent of GDP in domestic arrears, the overall cash deficit (including grants) more than doubled, from 2.9 percent of GDP to 6.5 percent, compared with some 5.3 percent of GDP initially projected under the program.4  

10. Revenues in 1999 were adversely affected by the energy crisis and transportation difficulties. Tax revenues were 15 percent below initial projections and even below the level of 1998, as significant shortfals were registered in most categories of direct and indirect taxation. The energy-crisis-related deterioration in the cash-flow situation of many enterprises led to the accumulation during the first half of the year of significant domestic tax arrears, still not collected by year's-end. There was a l6 percent decline in customs receipts, due to both smaller import volumes and lower effciency at the customs services. However, nontax revenues were 50 percent higher than expected (Table 4), and steps were taken to strengthen the efficiency of the domestic tax administration.  

11. Current expenditures reached 9.3 percent of GDP in 1999, roughly as projected. Spending in the priority sectors increased by 17 percent but nonetheless was below the programmed level, owing in part to the slowness of the budgetary procedures for committing these outlays. Spending on wages and the military was in line with the budget, while current outlays on goods and supplies were marginally above projected levels. Commitments of capital spending, though falling short of objectives, rose by 16 percent over the previous year to the equivalent of 9.6 percent of GDP.%  

12. The government repaid a net total of CFAF 4.9 billion in domestic payments arrears in 1999, following a similar reduction in 1998, and outstanding wage arrears have now been fully cleared. The overall deficit was financed by external project loans and program support from multilateral donors and France, as well as by an increase in net domestic credit from the banking system.?  

13.The public finance outcome was broadly in line with the program's objectives for the first quarter of 20o0. The program's targets for the current primary balance and net domestic credit to the government (adjusted for the shortfall in external financing relative to the program) were met, although the performance criterion on the net reduction in domestic arrears was not observed.  

14. Despite the resurgence of the energy crisis in the first months of the year and the interruption in fuel supplies, total revenue at end-March 2000 was slightly higher than programmed, although its composition was different than expected. Customs revenues fell short of the targeted level, owing primarily to smaller import volumes, and corporate income tax receipts were weak; however, the yield of the new value-added tax (VAT) introduced on January 1, 2000 was satisfactory, and nontax revenues were higher than anticipated, though this effect cannot be expected to continue.  

15.The government continued to maintain firm control over current spending. Outlays for wages and on the military were as programmed, but spending in the priority sectors was again considerably lower than planned. Moreover, to provide some liquidity support to the financially strapped electricity and water company (STEE) and enable it to meet the higher quarter, with much of the actual spending from the end of one fiscal year spilling over into the beginning of the next.  

6 Over the past five years, over 60 percent of public investment on average has been concentrated in the areas of agriculture and infrastructure, including transport, and 22 percent in health, education, and social affairs. The share of domestically financed investment in total capital spending rose to about 5 percent in 1998-99, from less than 1 percent in 199497. 7 While net credit from the central bank (including the counterpart of disbursements from the Fund) increased, there was a decrease in net credit from commercial banks-in August, the government shifted most of the treasury's deposits built up at the central bank through the disbursement of external financing to the commercial banks to provide liquidity support (see paragraph 15). These deposits were gradually drawn down in the last quarter of the year. 8 This outcome reflected delays in commiting outlays in health and education, owing in part to delays in mobilizing the external financing that funds a large portion of government spending in these areas, including the requirement of an audit of past spending financed by the European Union.  

cost of imported fuel, the government made advance payments on its electricity bills. All in all, the current primary deficit for the first quarter was CFAF 1.1 billion, as against the target of CFAF 3.6 billion. Investment spending was a litte over one-half of the programmed level, owing to difficulties encountered in mobilizing external project grants.  

16. Because of the advance payments of electricity bills and the nonreimbursement by the sugar company (SONASUT) of debt service paid on its behalf, the cash-flow situation during the first quarter was tight; there was a small increase in domestic arrears to local suppliers, instead of the programmed net reduction of CFAF 2 billion. Still the overall deficit (on a cash basis and including external grants) thus was limited to CFAF 10.4 billion (compared with CFAF 23.1 billion in the program). The deficit was financed, in the absence of external disbursements, by further recourse to central bank advances and an additional drawdown of treasury deposits. Nonetheless, the program's ceiling on net domestic bank credit (adjusted for the shortfall in external financing relative to the program) was observed, and Chad remained current on its external obligations.  

# C. Money and Credit  

17. Broad money declined by 2.6 percent in 1999. Moderate increases in money demand during the first half of the year gave way to declines in the last two quarters, tracking the pattern of the extension and reimbursement of credit for the cotton season. Domestic credit expanded by the equivalent of 10.7 percent of beginning-of-period broad money at end-1998, and the net foreign assets of the banking system fell by the equivalent of 5.4 percent of beginning-of-period broad money in 1999 (Table 6). The central bank's net external position declined sharply during l999 despite an upward surge in the second quarter, reflecting external disbursements and the repatriation of cotton export proceeds. By contrast, the net foreign assets position of the commercial banks, which had declined during most of the year, surged in November, when an external government loan held in a foreign bank was transferred to the accounts of two of the domestic banks.  

18. The development of net domestic credit in the latter half of 1999 was largely driven by net bank credit to the government. The bunching of external disbursements in the middle of the year permitted a reduction in the stock of central bank advances and a buildup of some CFAF 18 billion in deposits at the central bank by end-June. In July, CFAF 15 billion of these deposits were transferred to three commercial banks to provide a measure of liquidity support. As no further external financing was mobilized in the fourth quarter, the government gradually drew down these deposits and increased its recourse to central bank advances by CFAF 5 billion to CFAF 10.1 billion at year's end, thus ending 1999 in much the same position as it had started.  

19. The money stock increased by over ll percent in the first quarter of 2000, driven by the expansion of currency in circulation, which, in turn, was linked to the late start of the cotton season. Domestic credit expanded by 12.4 percent of beginning-of-period money stock, as the treasury drew down its deposits in the commercial banks, and credit was extended to finance the cotton crop. Credit to the rest of the economy declined, however, reflecting the ongoing efforts by the banks to consolidate their balance sheets and collect nonperforming loans The net foreign assets of the banking system as a whole fell during the. quarter, owing primarily to the decline in the net external position of the commercial banks.l0  

20. Although the financial situation of Chad's commercial banks has improved steadily over the past three years, by mid-1999 the banks were experiencing a short-term liquidity crunch, linked in part to a drain on reserves due to the decline in the volume and price of cotton exports. In July 1999, therefore, the govermment transferred'some CFAF 15 billion in treasury deposits from the central bank to three of the six commercial banks to provide a measure of short-term liquidity support.' These deposits were drawn down over the next few months to finance the government's deficit, but efforts by the banks to recover some of their nonperforming loans were relatively successful, enabling them to reduce their provisions and strengthen their liquidity and solvency positions. At end-December 1999, five of the six banks were in full compliance with the prudential ratios of the regional banking commission (COBAC) (see Table 10).  

# D. External Sector Developments1?  

21. The external current account (including official grants) widened by $3\%$ percentage points to the equivalent of 12.7 percent of GDP (14.3 percent, excluding grants) in 1999 (Table 7). Exports fell by 16 percent as receipts from cotton plunged-—both volumes and international prices dropped sharply. The value of imports declined by some 6 percent, reflecting the lower level of overall activity and a one-month transport strike during the year. The widening trade deficit was aggravated by a sharp drop in official nonproject grants, while the deficit of the services account was roughly unchanged at 11 percent of GDP.  

22. The capital account strengthened somewhat in 1999, reflecting primarily the increase in medium- and long-term government external borrowing, while medium- and long-term private capital flows were of the same order of magnitude as the previous year. There was however, a sharp turnaround in short-term private flows, corresponding to the increase in net foreign assets of commercial banks toward the end of the year. The overall deficit thus widened from CFAF 13.2 billion in 1998 to CFAF 20.4 billion in 1999, and was financed by a reduction in net official reserves of the central bank and the last drawing under the third annual Enhanced Structural Adjustment Facility (ESAF) arrangement.  

23. Debt-service payments amounted to CFAF 21.1 billion in 1999 (2.2 percent of GDP and 31 percent of tax revenue), up from CFAF 15.3 billion in 1998. Remaining external payments arrears were eliminated in 1998.1' 70 percent of the debt service was paid to multilateral creditors. A considerable share of these payments concerns debts contracted by the government and on-lent to public enterprises.'\* Of the CFAF 700 billion in public and publicly guaranteed debt outstanding at end-1999, 83 percent was owed to multilateral creditors, of which 55.5 percent to the Bretton Woods institutions).  

24. Chad's import tariff system is governed by the common external tariff (CET)of the CEMAC which has four tariff rates--5 percent for essential goods; 10 percent for raw materials and capital goods; 20 percent for intermediate goods; and 30 percent for final consumer goods. Imports from countries within the CEMAC zone are free of import duties, and all imports are subject to a 2.5 percent statistical tax. There are no quantitative restrictions on imports. The average effective import tariff rate in 1999 is estimated at some 18 percent. The major remaining exemption to the tariff system is the exemption of diesel imports by the STEE for electricity generation. A duty of 3 percent is levied on exports of animal products (livestock and skins), in addition to the statistical tax.  

# Box 1: Revisions of the Balance of Payments  

The present mission, in conjunction with the STA mission that visited N'Djamena at the same time, assisted the authorities in making a thorough revision of Chad's balance of payments estimates for the period 1994-97,based on the official balance of payments statistics that were made available to the team. Previous balance of payments estimates had been based on the oficial data as of 1994, and projections have been updated annually.   
The principal revisions concern the folowing (see Table 8): lower non-oil imports (a lower level of formal imports, but a higher level of informal imports); lower net income (as a result of lower compensation of employees); oicial current and capital transfers (estimated on the basis of questionnaires sent to donors and other offcials to evaluate the allcation of public funds); short-term capital movements (estimated on the basis of bank transactions and cross-checked with monetary accounts); reserves (which now include the revisions made by the Bank of Central African States (BEAC) after sorting banknotes). The revised balance of payments is now presented in a form consistent with the official balance of payments prepared by the BEAC, with more detail in the capital and financial account.   
As a result, the external current account deficit (including official transfers)for l999 is now estimated at 12.8 percent of GDP. instead of 17.4 percent of GDP.  

# E. Structural Reforms'5  

25.In the area of structural reform, the privatization of the SONASUT was completed on April 10, 2000, and the preparations for the privatization of the telecommunications company and the road maintenance company are well advanced. The implementation of the agreement reached on January 28, 2000 for privatizing the management of the STEE will begin shortly, after the agreement reached in mid-June on the treatment of the STEE's shortterm domestic debt, for which the government has assumed responsibility (see Box 2).16 Apart from the delays caused by the late start of the externally financed audit of COTONTCHAD, the other aspects of the cotton sector reform are proceeding on schedule. Official prices for petroleum products were adjusted upward in February to reflect world market conditions, and a committee was created to make timely future adjustments in light of procurement prices.'7 A mechanism for financing road maintenance was agreed on with donors, and legislation creating a new Road Maintenance Fund (FER) was submitted to the National Assembly in May 20o0. Drafts of the planned revisions to the civil service statutes to permit a merit-based promotion and remuneration system and a voluntary departure program have been prepared. These will be submitted to parliament after public discussion, as will the revised Social Security Code. Moreover, in January 20o0, the Chadian parliament adopted two anticorruption laws. Finally, the government completed the survey of statistical activity in Chad, thus respecting the relevant performance criterion at end-March.  

14 For example, almost 20 percent of the debt service paid inthe first quarter of 2000 was on behalf of the sugar company, SONASUT.  

15 Details of theimplementation ofthe structuralreform programare presented in the attached memorandum of economic and financial policies (Appendix I).  

16 Nonetheless, in view of the extreme dilapidation of the STEE's generating equipment, a period of at least five to six months will be required before a return to normal production levels could be envisaged.  

17 It is difficult to judge the impactof this measure ondomesticpricesand supplies, given the unsettled situation of the domestic market for petroleum products, including the interruption of imports from and through Cameroon in April 2000.  

18 The first creates aHighCourt of Justice with jurisdictionover cases of misuse of public funds and corruption, while the second establishes financial and penal sanctions for misuse of public funds, acts of corruption, extortion, and abuse of public office.  

# Box 2. Reform of the Energy Sector in Chad  

# A. The water and electric company (STEE)  

The January agreement provides for the private management of the STEE for a period of two years and a program of rehabilitation and investment (first phase),following which the private partner would take over majority ownership of the company (second phase). The agreement reached in early June 2000 on the repayment modalities for the STEE's short-term debt, which are now considered as government arrears and included in the table of financial operations (TOFE), foresees: (i) the immediate cash repayment of 25 percent of the amount (CFAF 2.5 bilion), financed by the net proceeds of the SONASUT privatization; and (ii) the issue of discountable medium-term treasury bonds for the remainder (CFAF 6.2 billion),to be repaid in equal installments over five or six years, with a two- or three-year grace period on the principal. Interest would be paid at the normal discount rate of the central bank.  

This transaction would affect the fiscal program in three ways: (i) an immediate increase in arrears repayment in the second quarter, and the rephasing of the repayment of other programmed arrears; (ii) a larger cash deficit, financed by the use of the SONASUT privatization proceeds and an increase in nonbank domestic financing; and (ii to the extent that the nonbank creditors discount the medium-term bonds, an increase in net domestic credit to the government. This increase in domestic bank financing would not represent a weakening of the fiscal adjustment, and the programmed repayment of arrears in 2000 would still take place, although later in the year than originally planned.  

# B.Accelerating domestic production  

The government has also decided to accelerate the construction of a pipeline from the Sedigi oil fieid to supply a privately financed oil refinery.This project, which was originally part of the Doba pipeline project, is expected to cover most of Chad's domestic requirements when it is completed in 2002. The government's (US\$34 million for the cost of the pipeline and the preparation of the construction site for the private refinery) will be financed using funds from an already acquired project loan from Taiwan, Province of China.  

# C. The Doba pipeline project  

The pipeline project involves (i) the development of oil reserves in the Doba region of southern Chad (the field system), with an investment of about US\$1.5 billion to exploit reserves of about 900 million barrels, entirely financed by a consortium of private oil companies; sand (i) the construction, operation, and ownership of a $1,100{\mathrm{km}}$ pipeline from Chad to the Cameroon coast by two joint-venture companies, TOTCO in Chad, and COTCO in Cameroon (the export system). The export system entails an investment of some USS300 million for TOTCO and US\$1,700 million for COTCO, for which external financing, including from the World Bank and the IFC, is being sought.The Chadian government's equity share in TOTCO and COTCO (15 and 5 percent, respectively) is being partly financed by the World Bank under a project approved on June 6, 2000.  

The construction and development phase will take 3-4 years, and oil exports are expected to begin in mid-2004. Oil receipts are projected to increase overall revenue in Chad by as much as a third--the use of the additional revenue is governed by the Oil Revenue Management Law of l998, and the implementation of the Law monitored by the parliament and domestic civil society groups, as wellas an International Advisory Group that will report regularly to the President of the World Bank.  

The revenue stream will be managed as follows: (i) petroleum revenues net of financing costs will be channeled through audited off-shore escrow accounts; (ii) 10 percent of royalties and dividends (about 85 percent of total revenues in the first ten years)willbe invested with an external financial institution in long-term investment instruments (the Future Generations Fund), and 90 percent will transit through special treasury accounts in one or two local commercial banks (the Special Petroleum Revenue Accounts) and used to finance incremental expenditures in the five priority sectors relating to poverty reduction; distribution to the producing region, and recurrent government expenditures. Revenues which cannot be used efficiently for the agreed objectives, or the mobilization of which would jeopardize macroeconomic stability, would be sterilized under arrangements agreed on with the Bank.  

26. The energy crisis and the uncertain supply of imported petroleum products have had a considerable adverse effect on production, transportation, and the critical import sector. As a result, the economic outlook for the rest of this year, as well as the capacity to maintain the fiscal adjustment effort, depends critically on the government's ability to resolve these difficulties.9 The priority, therefore, is to prevent any interruptions in supply from leading to immediate energy crises, such as Chad has experienced in recent years. The staff concurred with the authorities and donors on the pressing need for the constitution of adequate security stocks of petroleum products. Achieving this objective, which may be beyond reach in the short term will require close cooperation between the government and all participants in the sector.20  

# A. Fiscal Policy  

27. As noted above, the likely persistence of energy shortages for at least the next fivesix months is likely to have a negative impact on overallproduction, and to exacerbate the shortfalls in certain revenue categories, particularly import taxes and corporate income taxes (see Box 3). Moreover, the requirements to repay in cash a portion of the STEE debt further complicates the cash-flow situation. As a result, the quarterly targets of the program for the remainder of the year as regards revenues, the primary balance, the repayment of domestic arrears, and net domestic bank credit have had to be revised on the basis of the agreed methodology of the treasury cash flow plan (see Appendix I, Table 1, and Box 3). On the basis of identified external financing and sharply higher domestic financing, there remains a residual financing gap of CFAF 7.4 billion, which is expected to be fully covered by new adjustment lending from the Worid Bank and the African Development Bank. The mission stressed the need for the authorities to carefully and realistically monitor effective revenue mobilization, while ensuring that allocations for expenditure follow the agreed criteria (in particular, there must be adequate allocations for spending that cannot be compressed, such as wages, and electricity and water consumption). Control over the wage bill should be facilitated by the verification of employment records in the context of the harmonization of the civil service personnel and payroll files.

28. An analysis of the structure of revenue in Chad reveals its heavy reliance on a handful of large enterprises. The authorities have agreed to gradually transfer formal responsibility for the collection of domestic taxes from the treasury to the Tax Directorate (DIT).2' In addition, for large enterprises in the formal sector that maintain appropriate accounting systems and are in full compliance with their tax obligations, the authorities have decided to apply any credit balances on the 4 percent advance (acompte) toward the interim corporate income tax payment (tiers provisionnel) due during the current year, pending revision of the legislation in the next budget law.22 The authorities confirmed their intention to continue to implement the measures proposed by the IMF technical assistance mission at the end of 1999,2 in order to strengthen the efficiency of the tax administration and ensure better coverage of smalland medium-sized enterprises, individuals, and the informal sector, where there is a considerable tax potential that has not been adequately harnessed (as borne out by the results of the taxpayer identification and tax collection commissions).24 The mission also encouraged the authorities to implement as soon as possible the recruitment and training plan set up by the Tax Directorate.  

29. The decline in customs receipts since l998 partly reflects the resurgence of fraud and points to the need to strengthen customs inspection. The mission recommended the prompt formulation of an action plan to reduce fraud and improve inspection procedures and as quickly as possible called for the installation of the SYDONlA customs information system. The authorities agreed to step up efforts to mobilize the necessary external and domestic resources for this project. They also noted their intention to abide by the planned schedule for the reduction of the import reference price for imported sugar, as foreseen in the privatization agreement for the sugar company, and to resist pressures to renew the exceptional import tariff surcharge.  

30. On the expenditure side, the,mission commended the authorities on maintaining control of current spending but expressed concern at the delays in executing social expenditures. It therefore urged the authorities to reform the cumbersome public procurement procedures as soon as possible---in future, the preparation of procurement documents should begin well before the anticipated date of the callfor bids. The technical preparations for streamlining the expenditure management system and computerizing treasury operations are expected to be largely completed by the end of the year as planned, with the support of the IMF's resident treasury expert. These measures, together with the treasury cash-flow plan, should help ensure that projected expenditures, including in the priority social sectors, can be executed as planned. However, the review of government expenditure that was scheduled to start in March 2000 with the support of the World Bank has still not begun. The mission stressed the importance of this review as a means of enhancing the effciency of public expenditures, particularly in the context of implementing the poverty reduction strategy, and urged the authorities to work closely with World Bank staff to ensure that the review was launched as soon as possible. In the meantime, the government should also expedite the introduction of a mechanism for comparing expenditur commitments and actual expenditures in the education sector (originally foreseen for June 2000) as a source of information on the efficiency and effective targeting of these expenditures.  

31. Following the signing of the agreement with the newly reconstituted consortium that will build the Chad-Cameroon pipeline, the authorities received in May 2000 a transfer of US\$25 million from these partners. The government has decided to apply the rules of the oil revenue management law (signed in l998) to the use of these funds. As such, the money will be spent in the priority areas of health, education, rural development, and transportation, and will be fully consistent with the priorities identified in the interim PRSP. The concerned ministries are presently setting out detailed spending plans, and the authorities have stressed that this spending will be in addition to the existing budget allocations for these priority sectors, and willbe committed only if they can be efficiently absorbed. The mission commended the authorities on this transparent approach. It was agreed that the spending expected from this source in 2000 would be included in the table of government financial operations only when the detailed spending plans have been completed.25  

32. Based on the revised projections of available resources and priority expenditures in the treasury cash-flow plan, the level of public investment for 20oo has been adjusted downward, reflecting the likely delays in mobilizing the domestic counterpart of foreignfinanced public investment. The mission urged the authorities to minimize these delays, so as to make fullest possible use of the development resources committed by Chad's external partners. While agreeing in principle, the authorities saw little scope for compressing other expenditure to provide more funds for the local counterpart of foreign-financed investment. In particular, they were reluctant to substitute the above-mentioned resources from the oil consortium for budgeted social spending and use these budgetary resources for investment financing, arguing that this would reduce the transparency of the use of these funds.  

33. Finally, the authorities underscored their commitment to complete the programmed repayment of domestic arrears by the end of the year, including the reimbursement of arrears to COTONTCHAD that was agreed as part of the financial support package at the start of the last crop season. However, the repayments willtake place later in the year than envisaged, owing to the need to give priority to the cash payment required in the context of the proposed treatment of STEE's short-term debt. The authorities confirmed that the verification of outstanding domestic arrears would be completed by end-September as planned, and a comprehensive repayment plan formulated in time for the next fiscal year.  

# B. Money and Credit  

34.The success of the banks' effort to recover nonperforming ioans, including through the judicial system, has considerably strengthened their financial position over the last six months. In discussions with the monetary authorities and the commercial banks, the mission urged that this effort be stepped up, so as to complete the process of rehabilitation of the banks. At the same time, the banks would benefit from a more aggressive and innovative  

diversification of their financial resource base, so as to afford protection against the volatility of the short-term deposits of the public sector. The treasury should also make an effort to distribute its deposits more equitably among the banks and ensure that their use does not destabilize the banks' cash flow, which, despite the recent improvement, is stillprecarious. The banks noted, however, that a diversification of their resource base and lending activities would be very difficult.26 The mobilization of private deposits suffered from a general lack of confidence in the banking system, which resulted from the freezing or loss of private deposits during the deep banking crisis at the start of the 199Os. Moreover, the low level of financial savings in Chad and the general volatility of public sector deposits (including those linked to foreign-financed investment projects) made maturity transformation difficult, given the supervisory regulations on risk exposure. The banks also suggested that the diversification of lending activities could be facilitated by the creation of a loan guarantee structure, enabling them to lend to borrowers lacking the required collateral. The staff considered that the proposal warranted careful consideration, but advised against any form of government involvement, as this would be inconsistent with the state's withdrawal from bank management and credit decisions, and could open the door to abuse of the system.  

35. In this context, the mission urged the authorities to complete the study of an appropriate strategy for monitoring and supervising microfinance institutions, promoting small-scale savings, and financing microprojects in urban and rural areas that are generally not financed by the commercial banks. A gradual integration of microfinance institutions into the formal financial system could enable these institutions to obtain the additional financing from commercial banks and invest their deposits on more favorable terms.  

36.In the area of regional monetary policy, the authorities noted an improvement in the volume and efficiency of transactions on the local interbank market, as well as in the efficiency of transfers between the central bank and commercial banks, and between local banks and their foreign correspondents. They expressed satisfaction with the improvement in the financial situation of the banks, which they considered a direct result of the enhanced surveillance by the regional banking commission. Both the monetary authorities and the commercial banks expected that the new accounting framework for banks in the Central African Economic and Monetary Community (CEMAC), introduced in early 2000, and the start of the CERBER project (the collection of the requisite statements from the banks and financial institutions for processing, followed by their return to the institutions) would further improve the transparency of bank operations and facilitate bank supervision.  

# C. Structural Reforms?  

37. The mission commended the authorities on the progress made in recent months in implementing various structural reforms, particularly in the area of privatizing the remaining major public enterprises (sugar, telecommunications, water and electricity, and road maintenance). However, it regretted that neither the privatization agreement for the sugar company nor the approach envisaged for the privatization of the telecommunications company would allow for the actual recovery of the sizable tax arrears of these two enterprises.  

38.The mission welcomed the agreement reached with the World Bank on funding routine road maintenance, which is essential for mobilizing donor resources to extend the road network. However, it recommended that the part of the petroleum taxes earmarked for the FER be converted into a user fee, so that tax revenues are not collected by agencies other than the treasury.  

39. In the area of petroleum product pricing, the decision to adjust prices at the pump on the basis of import prices is an important step. However, given the impossibility of regulating the domestic market using official prices,28 the mission urged the government to move to liberalize prices completely as soon as possible-a more rational pricing policy could help improve the supply on the domestic market, although it would not, on its own, suffice to guarantee a regular supply.  

40. The various reforms of the public administration are well under way. The mission urged the authorities to complete as quickly as possible the preparatory work for harmonizing the civil service personnel and payroll records, and to proceed apace with the revision of the civil service statutes to allow for merit-based remuneration and advancement, and voluntary early departure programs. In view of their importance in managing the wage bill and in the process of administrative decentralization currently being worked on, every effort should be made to complete this work in time for the next budget.  

41. With regard to the administrative decentralization process, the laws recently promulgated on the local governments and their electoral system allow them to borrow directly, both domestically and abroad. Officials of the ministry of finance shared the mission's concern that such borrowing could lead to financial slippages, and stressed that the government would ensure that the implementing provisions for these laws establish very  

precise, restrictive benchmarks for the budgetary equilibrium of these governments. In step with the civil service reform, the mission also underscored the importance of completing the various preparatory steps for the effective decentralization of functional authority set out in the program.  

42. The mission noted the recent improvements in the justice system,29 and urged the authorities to convene regular meetings of the Joint Public-Private Sector Commission on Judicial Reform to guide these efforts. Finally, the mission welcomed the progress in finalizing the revision to the social security code, which is due to be submitted to the National Assembly before year's end, thus allowing for the preparation in 200l of a plan to rehabilitate the social security system.  

43. The mission underscored the critical importance of maintaining the momentum of reform in the cotton sector and, in particular, reaching a decision on the strategy for the divestiture of the government's interests in the sector by end-September, as planned. The authorities noted that the delay in completing the financial rehabilitation plan was due only to the late mobilization of the necessary external financing, and that it would be adopted before Board consideration of the program review. The plan was essential to arresting the financial decline of the enterprise and facilitating its eventual privatization.30 The nomination of the controller-general was likely to take somewhat longer, however, given the need to observe standard recruitment procedures, but it would be completed as a prior condition of the second review of the program.  

44. The mission welcomed the authorities' decision to strengthen the country's statistical system and increase the budgetary resources allocated to statistical activities, as recommended by the recent STA mission. This strengthening assumes particular importance in the context of the preparation of the PRSP.  

# D. Poverty Reduction Strategy  

45.A joint Fund/Bank mission in early March 2oo0 discussed with the Chadian authorities and representatives of civil society and the donor community the concept and objectives of a national poverty reduction strategy (NPRS), which is expected to build on the sectoral priorities established during the 1998 Geneva Round Table. The authorities have since created a Steering Committee composed of representatives of the key government ministries, civil society, the press, the private sector, and political institutions to oversee the preparation of the poverty reduction strategy paper (PRSP).3' A seminar to launch the process was organized from April 25 to April 27, 2000, at which over 200 representatives of civil society and the administration decided, in a participatory environment, on the methodology, timetable, and next steps in the preparation of the NPRS. An interim poverty reduction strategy paper (interim PRSP) has been prepared under the direction of the Steering Committee, including the budget and the timetable of activities leading up to the completion of the definitive PRSP in June 2001.  

46. With regard to the PRSP process, the staff stressed the importance of carefully defining the cost of the consultative process; it also urged the authorities to assume a part of the budget for the Steering Committe's activities. The authorities confirmed their intention to seek commitments of technical and financial assistance from their partners,² and to consult with the Bretton Woods institutions on the PRSP preparation.  

47. With regard to possible assistance under the enhanced Initiative for Heavily Indebted Poor Countries (HIPC Initiative), the authorities wish to base the conditionality for the floating completion point on measurable progress in the priority social areas, and intend to define quantified intermediate objectives for inclusion in the conditionality. They also intend to begin preparing spending plans for using the additional resources from debt relief in the priority areas as they have already done with the transfer received from the oil companies. The mission welcomed this approach and stressed the need to begin work as soon as possible on the costing of poverty-reducing measures in the key sectors for inclusion in next year's budget.  

# IV. STAFF APPRAISAL  

48. Chad has made satisfactory progress in implementing the first annual PRGFsupported program, approved on January 7, 2000. The fiscal outturn at end-March was broadly in line with the program's targets, although the composition of revenue and expenditure differed somewhat from expectations and the tight cash-flow situation prevented the targeted reduction of domestic payments arrears.  

49. Chad's economic prospects are clouded by recurrent energy crises. The staff shares the authorities' view that finding a lasting solution to this problem must be one of the govermment's priorities in the near term and, therefore, welcomes the decision to introduce more flexibility into the official petroleum pricing system. However, a rational policy aimed at maintaining adequate security stocks of petroleum products must also be formulated as soon as possible, in full consultation with all participants in the sector.  

50.The impact of the energy crisis on economic activity and government revenue constitutes the major risk to the program for the rest of the year, and has necessitated a revision of the revenue and primary balance targets. The resulting cash-flow difficulties underscore the importance of the treasury cash- flow plan as a tool for safeguarding the fiscal program. Effective revenue mobilization must thus be continually monitored, and the government should be prepared to adjust expenditure commitments immediately if the situation warrants this. In particular, careful management of the government's deposits in the banking system is needed.  

51.To reinforce revenue collection, the new customs information system, SYDONIA, should be implemented as soon as possible as a much-needed anchor for efforts to combat fraud and enhance efficiency in the customs administration. Ongoing efforts to strengthen the tax administration, which have shown positive results, should be accelerated, including by an increase in the human and material resources assigned to the Tax Directorate. The staff also urges the authorities to resist any pressures to increase the protection of the domestic sugar market, and to explore the possibility of accelerating the schedule for eliminating the system of import reference prices for sugar.  

52. On the expenditure side, the shortfall in social spending and in public investment in the first quarter of 2000 is worrisome, particularly given Chad's pressing needs. The mission thus urges the authorities to make every effort to mobilize the necessary domestic counterpart of foreign-financed investment spending, so as to take fulladvantage of donors' willingness to contribute to Chad's development effort, and to press ahead with the planned revision of public procurement procedures, so as to permit a “catching up" of social expenditures later in the year as the cash-flow situation eases.  

53.The mission commends the authorities on their approach to using the transfer received from the petroleum consortium. This decision is a further sign of their commitment to use the resources from the exploitation of the petroleum resources to accelerate economic and social development and the reduction of poverty. The preparation of detailed spending plans will also aid the authorities in the effort to provide detailed cost estimates of the poverty reduction measures to be included in the budget.  

54. In the area of money and credit, the staff notes the improvement in the liquidity and solvency position of the banks, but the dependence of the commercial banks on relatively volatile government deposits for loanable resources continues to limit their ability to diversify their lending and provide longer-term credit. The banks' proposal for creating a loan guarantee structure should be carefully considered, but the staff advises against direct government involvement in such a scheme. An appropriate strategy for promoting the development of microfinance should therefore be defined promptly as a means of promoting small-scale savings and providing small-scale enterprises and rural farmers with access to credit on affordable terms.  

55. The authorities have made considerable progress in implementing structural reforms over the last few months, particularly in the area of privatization and in preparing the reform of the civil service. This momentum should be maintained; in particular, the civil service reforms should be enacted in time for the next budget, if possible, so as to further enhance the government's ability to manage its human resources and the wage bill rationally and efficiently. Equally important is the continuation of the reform of the cotton sector, which, given its importance as a source of cash income for a considerable part of the rural population, should also be a central element of the poverty reduction strategy.  

56.The staff reiterates the importance of ensuring that the process of administrative decentralization now under way does not weaken overallfinancial discipline. The authorities should be vigilant in preventing a duplication of efforts or an undue expansion of public sector employment, and it is essential that the budgets of local administrations be subject to strict control, including limits on their ability to finance deficits.  

57. The authorities have made a good start to the preparation of the national poverty reduction strategy. The consultative approach followed in preparing the interim PRSP augurs wellfor the degree of participation that will underpin the final strategy. The process is ambitious, however; the authorities should therefore ensure that the Steering Committee is promptly provided with the human and material resources it needs to accomplish its mission. They should also quickly identify areas where assistance is required (financial or technical) from their development partners and seek firm commitments from donors. The authorities could draw on the conclusions of the recent multisector statistics mission to help determine their requirements for financial and technical assistance to improve the compilation and dissemination of macroeconomic statistics, sociodemographic indicators, and other data needed to monitor progress.  

58. The authorities have made a relatively good start to their new three-year program supported by the PRGF. While three performance criteria for end-March were missed, these were for the most part due to exogenous factors. The treasury cash-flow plan was adopted in April; the financial rehabilitation plan for COTONTCHAD has been adopted and a time limit set for the recruitment of the controller-general; and a revised repayment plan for the domestic arrears has been established that will allow the reimbursement of the originally programmed amounts by the end of the year. The authorities have also made substantial progress in structural reforms and continue to demonstrate their commitment to the implementation of the program. The staff therefore recommends that the Executive Board grant the requested waivers and conclude the first review of the first annual arrangement under the PRGF.  

# V PROPOSED DECISION  

The following draft decision is proposed for adoption by the Executive Board:  

1. Chad has consulted with the Fund in accordance with paragraph 2(e) of the three-year arrangement for Chad under the Poverty Reduction and Growth Facility (PRGF) (EBS/99/234, Supplement 1), and paragraph 6 of the letter dated November 12, 1999 from the Minister of Economy and Finance.  

2. The letter from the Minister of Finance dated July 6, 2000 with its attached memorandum and tables, shall be attached to the three-year PRGF arrangement for Chad, and the letter dated November 12, 1999 from the Minister of Economy and Finance with its attached memorandum, shall be read as supplemented by the letter dated July 6, 2000 and its attached memorandum and tables.  

3. Accordingly, the following provisions shall be added to the PRGF arrangement for Chad: (a) a new paragraph 1(cc) shall be added to read as follows:  

"During the second year of the arrangement, the third disbursement under the arrangement, in an amount equivalent to SDR 5.2 million, will be made available after January 15, 200l at the request of Chad and subject to paragraph 2 below."  

(b) A new paragraph 1(dd) shall be added to read as follows:  

"The phasing of, and the conditions for, further disbursements during the second year of the arrangement will be established in a review to be completed not later than January 15,2001."  

(c) A new paragraph 2(aa) shall be added to read as follows:  

"Chad will not request the disbursement of the third loan referred to in paragraph 1(cc) above, if the Managing Director of the Trustee finds that data as of end-September 2000 indicate that the ceilings and floors referred to in paragraph 2(a)(i) to (v) of this arrangement as specified in Table l of the Memorandum attached to the letter of July $\mathbf{6,}$ 2000.”  

(d) A new paragraph 2(ee) shall be added to read as follows:  

"Chad will not request the disbursement of the third loan referred to in paragraph 1(cc) above until the Trustee has determined that the second review referred to in paragraph 4 of the letter of July 6, 200 by the Minister of Finance has been completed.  

# 3. The Fund decides  

(i) that the review contemplated in paragraph 2(e) of the three-year PRGF   
arrangement for Chad has been completed notwithstanding the non-observance of the   
performance criteria specified in paragraph 2(a)(ii), 2(b)(i) and 2(b)(ii); and (ii) that the Interim Poverty Reduction Strategy Paper set forth in EBD/00/55   
provides a sound basis for the development of a fully participatory Poverty Reduction   
Strategy Paper, and for Fund concessional assistance under the PRGF arrangement.
